zone">Time zone</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/UTC%2B2" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+2">UTC+2</a> (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_European_Time" title="Eastern European Time">EET</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><span style="white-space:nowrap">&#160;\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;Summer (<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</span></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/UTC%2B3" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC+3">UTC+3</a> (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_European_Summer_Time" title="Eastern European Summer Time">EEST</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Postal code</th><td class="infobox-data adr"><div class="postal-code">4000</div></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">Area code(s)</a></th><td class="infobox-data">(+359) 032</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Car_plates" class="mw-redirect" title="Car plates">Car plates</a></th><td class="infobox-data">PB</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.plovdiv.bg/">www.plovdiv.bg</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Plovdiv</b> (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">\xd0\x9f\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb4\xd0\xb8\xd0\xb2</span>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Bulgarian" title="Help:IPA/Bulgarian">[\xcb\x88p\xc9\xab\xc9\x94vdif]</a></span>) is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_and_second_largest_cities_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="List of largest cities and second largest cities by country">second-largest city</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, standing on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Maritsa" title="Maritsa">Maritsa</a> river in the historical region of <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a>. It has a population of 346,893 as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> and 675,000 in the greater metropolitan area. Plovdiv is the cultural capital of Bulgaria and was the <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> in 2019. It is an important economic, transport, cultural, and educational center. During most of its <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">recorded history</a>, Plovdiv was known by the name <i><a href="/wiki/Philippopolis_(Thrace)" title="Philippopolis (Thrace)">Philippopolis</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text">\xce\xa6\xce\xb9\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\xcf\x80\xcf\x80\xce\xbf\xcf\x8d\xcf\x80\xce\xbf\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\xcf\x82</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Greek" title="Romanization of Greek">translit.</a></small>&#160;<i lang="grc-Latn" title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language romanization"><i>Philippo\xc3\xbapolis</i></i>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a></small>&#160;"Philip\'s city") after <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a>.\n</p><p>Plovdiv is situated in a fertile region of south-central Bulgaria on the two banks of the <a href="/wiki/Maritsa_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritsa River">Maritsa River</a>. The city has historically developed on seven <a href="/wiki/Syenite" title="Syenite">syenite</a> hills, some of which are 250 metres (820 feet) high. Because of these hills, Plovdiv is often referred to in Bulgaria as "The City of the Seven Hills". There is evidence of habitation in Plovdiv dating back to the 6th millennium BCE, when the first <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> settlements were established. The city was subsequently a <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a> settlement and later ruled by <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtic_settlement_of_Southeast_Europe" title="Celtic settlement of Southeast Europe">Celts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_people" title="Rus&#39; people">Rus\'</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_Empire" title="Latin Empire">Crusaders</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-plovdiv1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plovdiv1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Philippopolis was founded as a <i><a href="/wiki/Polis" title="Polis">polis</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Philip_the_Great" class="mw-redirect" title="Philip the Great">Philip the Great</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reigned">r</abbr>.&#160;359\xe2\x80\x93336&#160;BCE</span>), the king of ancient <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">Macedonia</a>, settling there both Thracians and 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Macedonians" title="Ancient Macedonians">Macedonians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greeks" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Greeks">Greeks</a> in 342 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Control of the city alternated between the Macedonian kingdom and the Thracian <a href="/wiki/Odrysian_kingdom" title="Odrysian kingdom">Odrysian kingdom</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic period</a>; the Macedonian king <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Macedon" title="Philip V of Macedon">Philip V</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reigned">r</abbr>.&#160;221\xe2\x80\x93179&#160;BCE</span>) reoccupied the city in 183 BCE and his successor <a href="/wiki/Perseus_of_Macedon" title="Perseus of Macedon">Perseus</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reigned">r</abbr>.&#160;179\xe2\x80\x93168&#160;BCE</span>) held the city with the Odrysians until the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> conquered the Macedonian kingdom in 168 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Philippopolis became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Thracia" title="Thracia">Thracia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The city was at the centre of the road network of inland Thrace, and the strategic <i><a href="/wiki/Via_Militaris" title="Via Militaris">Via Militaris</a></i> was crossed by several other roads at the site, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_emperor" title="Roman emperor">Roman emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius" title="Marcus Aurelius">Marcus Aurelius</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reigned">r</abbr>.&#160;161\xe2\x80\x93180&#160;CE</span>) built a new <a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">wall</a> around the city.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" class="mw-redirect" title="Late Antiquity">Late Antiquity</a>, Philippopolis was an important stronghold, but was sacked in 250 during the <a href="/wiki/Crisis_of_the_Third_Century" title="Crisis of the Third Century">Crisis of the Third Century</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> after the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Philippopolis_(250)" title="Siege of Philippopolis (250)">Siege of Philippopolis</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Cniva" title="Cniva">Cniva</a>.  After this the settlement contracted, though it remained a major city, with the city walls rebuilt and new Christian <a href="/wiki/Basilicas" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilicas">basilicas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_baths" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman baths">Roman baths</a> constructed in the 4th century.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The city was again sacked by the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a> in 441/442, and the walls were again rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Roman Philippopolis resisted another attack, by the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a> in the 580s, after the walls were renewed yet again by <a href="/wiki/Justinian_the_Great" class="mw-redirect" title="Justinian the Great">Justinian the Great</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reigned">r</abbr>.&#160;527\xe2\x80\x93565</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-:2_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, Philippopolis fell to the <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> of the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a> in 863, during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Boris_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Boris I">Boris I</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reigned">r</abbr>.&#160;852\xe2\x80\x93889</span>), having been briefly abandoned by the Christian inhabitants in 813 during a dispute with the <i><a href="/wiki/Khan_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Khan of Bulgaria">khan</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Krum" title="Krum">Krum</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reigned">r</abbr>.&#160;<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;803</span>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93&#160;814</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-:2_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Bulgarian_wars" title="Byzantine\xe2\x80\x93Bulgarian wars">Byzantine\xe2\x80\x93Bulgarian wars</a>, the emperor <a href="/wiki/Basil_the_Bulgar-Slayer" class="mw-redirect" title="Basil the Bulgar-Slayer">Basil the Bulgar-Slayer</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reigned">r</abbr>.&#160;960\xe2\x80\x931025</span>) used Philippopolis as a major strategic fortification, governed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Protospatharios" title="Protospatharios">protospatharios</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Nikephoros_Xiphias" title="Nikephoros Xiphias">Nikephoros Xiphias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In the middle 11th century, the city was attacked by the <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">Pechenegs</a>, who occupied it briefly around 1090.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The city continued to prosper, with the walls restored in the 12th century, during which the historian and politician <a href="/wiki/Niketas_Choniates" title="Niketas Choniates">Niketas Choniates</a> was its governor and the physician <a href="/wiki/Michael_Italikos" title="Michael Italikos">Michael Italikos</a> was its <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop" title="Metropolitan bishop">metropolitan bishop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> According to the Latin historian of the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_of_Villehardouin" title="Geoffrey of Villehardouin">Geoffrey of Villehardouin</a>, Philippopolis was the third largest city in the Byzantine Empire, after <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> (<a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Thessalonica" class="mw-redirect" title="Thessalonica">Thessalonica</a> (<a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It suffered damage from the armies passing through the city during the <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a> as well as from sectarian violence between the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Orthodox">Armenian Orthodox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paulician" class="mw-redirect" title="Paulician">Paulician</a> denominations.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The city was destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Kaloyan_of_Bulgaria" title="Kaloyan of Bulgaria">Kaloyan of Bulgaria</a> (<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><abbr title="reigned">r</abbr>.&#160;1196\xe2\x80\x931207</span>) in 1206 and rebuilt thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 1219, the city became the capital of the Crusader <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Philippopolis" title="Duchy of Philippopolis">Duchy of Philippopolis</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Empire" title="Latin Empire">Latin Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire" title="Second Bulgarian Empire">Second Bulgarian Empire</a> recovered the city in 1263, but lost it to Byzantine control before recapturing it in 1323.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> conquered Philippopolis (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Filibe</i>) in 1363 or 1364.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 January 1878, at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x931878)">Russo-Turkish War (1877\xe2\x80\x931878)</a>, Plovdiv was taken away from Ottoman rule by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian</a> army. It remained within the borders of Bulgaria until July of the same year, when it became the capital of the autonomous Ottoman region of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Rumelia" title="Eastern Rumelia">Eastern Rumelia</a>. In 1885, Plovdiv and Eastern Rumelia joined Bulgaria.\n</p><p>There are many preserved ruins such as the ancient <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Roman_theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Plovdiv Roman theatre">Plovdiv Roman theatre</a>, a Roman <a href="/wiki/Odeon_(building)" title="Odeon (building)">odeon</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Roman_aqueduct" title="Roman aqueduct">Roman aqueduct</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Roman_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Plovdiv Roman Stadium">Plovdiv Roman Stadium</a>, the archaeological complex Eirene, and others. Plovdiv is host to a huge variety of cultural events such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Fair_Plovdiv" title="International Fair Plovdiv">International Fair Plovdiv</a>, the international theatrical <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">festival</a> "A stage on a crossroad", the TV festival "The golden chest", and many more novel festivals, such as Night/Plovdiv in September, Kapana Fest, and Opera Open. The oldest American educational institution outside the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_College_of_Sofia" title="American College of Sofia">American College of Sofia</a>, was founded in Plovdiv in 1860 and later moved to Sofia.\n</p><p>On 5 September 2014, Plovdiv was selected as the Bulgarian host of the <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> 2019 alongside the Italian city of <a href="/wiki/Matera" title="Matera">Matera</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-culturecapital_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culturecapital-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> This happened with the help of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://plovdiv2019.eu/en/">Municipal Foundation "Plovdiv 2019\xe2\x80\xb3</a>, a non-government organization, which was established in 2011 by Plovdiv\'s City Council whose main objectives were to develop and to prepare Plovdiv\'s bid book for European Capital of Culture in 2019.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Literature"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Economic_Indicators"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Economic Indicators</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Industry"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Industry</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Shopping_and_commerce"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Shopping and commerce</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Sports_and_recreation"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sports and recreation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Notable_citizens"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Notable citizens</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#International_relations"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">International relations</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Twin_towns_\xe2\x80\x93_sister_cities"><span class="tocnumber">14.1</span> <span class="toctext">Twin towns \xe2\x80\x93 sister cities</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Honour"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Honour</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Gallery"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">Gallery</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teritoriul_onomastic_al_elementului_dava_-_Sorin_Olteanu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Teritoriul_onomastic_al_elementului_dava_-_Sorin_Olteanu.jpg/220px-Teritoriul_onomastic_al_elementului_dava_-_Sorin_Olteanu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Teritoriul_onomastic_al_elementului_dava_-_Sorin_Olteanu.jpg/330px-Teritoriul_onomastic_al_elementului_dava_-_Sorin_Olteanu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Teritoriul_onomastic_al_elementului_dava_-_Sorin_Olteanu.jpg/440px-Teritoriul_onomastic_al_elementului_dava_-_Sorin_Olteanu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="498" data-file-height="516" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teritoriul_onomastic_al_elementului_dava_-_Sorin_Olteanu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ancient settlements with names related to "deva". Pulpudeva denotes Plovdiv in which the latter name is rooted.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thraciae-veteris-typvs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Thraciae-veteris-typvs.jpg/220px-Thraciae-veteris-typvs.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Thraciae-veteris-typvs.jpg/330px-Thraciae-veteris-typvs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Thraciae-veteris-typvs.jpg/440px-Thraciae-veteris-typvs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4452" data-file-height="3424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thraciae-veteris-typvs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map describing the city as "Philippopolis, que et Poneropolis, Duloupolis, Eumolpiada, item Trimontium, at que Pulpudena"</div></div></div>\n<p>Plovdiv was given various names throughout its long history. The <a href="/wiki/Odrysian_kingdom" title="Odrysian kingdom">Odrysian</a> capital <i>Odryssa</i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\x9f\xce\x94\xce\xa1\xce\xa5\xce\xa3\xce\xa3\xce\x91</span>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">ODRYSSA</i></small>) is suggested to have been modern Plovdiv by numismatic research<sup id="cite_ref-arc_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arc-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Odrin" class="mw-redirect" title="Odrin">Odrin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-academia_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academia-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\nThe Greek historian <a href="/wiki/Theopompus" title="Theopompus">Theopompus</a><sup id="cite_ref-theopompi_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theopompi-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> mentioned it in the 4th century BCE as a town named <i>Poneropolis</i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\xa0\xce\x9f\xce\x9d\xce\x97\xce\xa1\xce\x9f\xce\xa0\xce\x9f\xce\x9b\xce\x99\xce\xa3</span></small> "town of villains") in pejorative relation to the conquest by king <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a> who is said to have settled the town with 2,000 men who were false-accusers, sycophants, lawyers, and other possible disreputables.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">Plutarch</a>, the town was named by this king after he had populated it with a crew of rogues and vagabonds,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> but this is possibly a folk name that did not actually exist.<sup id="cite_ref-academia_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academia-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The names <i>Dulon polis</i>  (<small><a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\x94\xce\x9f\xce\xa5\xce\x9b\xce\xa9\xce\x9d \xce\xa0\xce\x9f\xce\x9b\xce\x99\xce\xa3</span></small> "slaves\' town") and possibly <i>Moichopolis</i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\x9c\xce\x9f\xce\x99\xce\xa7\xce\x9f\xce\xa0\xce\x9f\xce\x9b\xce\x99\xce\xa3</span></small>  "adulterer\'s town") likely have similar origins.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The city has been called <i>Philippopolis</i> (<small>\xce\xa6\xce\x99\xce\x9b\xce\x99\xce\xa0\xce\xa0\xce\x9f\xce\xa0\xce\x9f\xce\x9b\xce\x99\xce\xa3</small> <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek" title="Help:IPA/Greek">[pilpopolis]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\xa6\xce\xb9\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\xcf\x80\xcf\x80\xce\xbf\xcf\x8d\xcf\x80\xce\xbf\xce\xbb\xce\xb7</span>, in modern Greek, <i>Philippoupoli</i> <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek" title="Help:IPA/Greek">[filipupoli]</a></span>) or "the city of Philip", from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Greek language">Greek</a> <i>Philippos</i> "horse-lover", most likely in honor of <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a><sup id="cite_ref-col_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-col-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> after his death or in honor of <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Macedon" title="Philip V of Macedon">Philip V</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-arc_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arc-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pld_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pld-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> as this name was first mentioned in the 2nd century BCE by <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">Polybius</a> in connection with the campaign of Philip V.<sup id="cite_ref-arc_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arc-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pld_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pld-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> <i>Philippopolis</i> was identified later by <a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">Plutarch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny</a> as the former <i>Poneropolis</i>. <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> identified Philip II\'s settlement of most "evil, wicked" (ponerotatus) as Calybe (<a href="/wiki/Kabyle_(ancient_city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabyle (ancient city)">Kabyle</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> whereas <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> considered the location of Poneropolis different than the rest.\n</p><p><i>Kendrisia</i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\x9a\xce\x95\xce\x9d\xce\x94\xce\xa1\xce\x95\xce\x99\xcf\xb9\xce\x95\xce\x99\xce\x91</span></small>) was an old name of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-plovdiv1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plovdiv1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Its earliest recorded use is on an artifact mentioning that king <a href="/wiki/Beithys" title="Beithys">Beithys</a>, priest of the Syrian goddess, brought gifts to Kendriso <a href="/wiki/Apollo" title="Apollo">Apollo</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> the deity is recorded to be named multiple times after different cities. Later Roman coins mentioned the name which is possibly derived from Thracian god Kendriso who is equated with Apollo,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Cedrus" title="Cedrus">cedar</a> forests, or from the Thracian tribe artifacts known as the kendrisi.<sup id="cite_ref-plovdiv1_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plovdiv1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pld_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pld-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Another assumed name is the 1st century CE <i>Tiberias</i> in honor of the Roman emperor <a href="/wiki/Tiberius" title="Tiberius">Tiberius</a>, under whom the <a href="/wiki/Odrysian_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Odrysian Kingdom">Odrysian Kingdom</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client</a> of Rome.<sup id="cite_ref-academia_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academia-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> After the Romans had taken control of the area, the city was named in <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">TRIMONTIUM</i>, meaning "The Three Hills", and mentioned in the 1st century by <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny</a>. At times the name was <i><a href="/wiki/Ulpia_gens" title="Ulpia gens">Ulpia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Flavia_gens" title="Flavia gens">Flavia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Julia_gens" title="Julia gens">Julia</a></i> after the Roman families.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ammianus_Marcellinus" title="Ammianus Marcellinus">Ammianus Marcellinus</a> wrote in the 4th century CE that the then city had been the old <i>Eumolpias</i>/<i>Eumolpiada,</i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">EVMOLPIAS, EVMOLPIADA</i></small>),<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> the oldest name chronologically.<sup id="cite_ref-academia_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academia-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It was named after the mythical Thracian king <a href="/wiki/Eumolpos" class="mw-redirect" title="Eumolpos">Eumolpos</a>, son of <a href="/wiki/Poseidon" title="Poseidon">Poseidon</a><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_(mythology)" title="Jupiter (mythology)">Jupiter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> who may have founded the city around 1200 BCE<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> or 1350 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> It is also possible that it was named after the <a href="/wiki/Vestal_Virgins" class="mw-redirect" title="Vestal Virgins">Vestal Virgins</a> in the temples \xe2\x80\x93 evmolpeya.<sup id="cite_ref-plovdiv1_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plovdiv1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 6th century CE, <a href="/wiki/Jordanes" title="Jordanes">Jordanes</a> wrote that the former name of the city was <i>Pulpudeva</i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">PVLPVDEVA</i></small>) and that <a href="/wiki/Philip_the_Arab" title="Philip the Arab">Philip the Arab</a> named the city after himself. This name is most likely a <a href="/wiki/Thracian_language" title="Thracian language">Thracian</a> oral translation<sup id="cite_ref-plovdiv1_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plovdiv1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> of the other as it kept all consonants of the name Philip + <a href="/wiki/Dava_(Dacian)" title="Dava (Dacian)">deva (city)</a>. Although the two names sound similar, they may not share the same origin as <a href="/wiki/Odrin" class="mw-redirect" title="Odrin">Odrin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adrianople" class="mw-redirect" title="Adrianople">Adrianople</a> do, and <i>Pulpudeva</i> may have predated the other names<sup id="cite_ref-uk_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uk-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> meaning "lake city" in <a href="/wiki/Thracian_language" title="Thracian language">Thracian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pld_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pld-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Since the 9th century CE the Slavic name began to appear as <i>Papaldiv/n, Plo(v)div, Pladiv, Pladin, Plapdiv, Plovdin,</i> which originate from <i>Pulpudeva</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> As a result, the name has lost any meaning. In British English the Bulgarian variant <i>Pl\xc3\xb2vdiv</i> has become prevalent after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Crusaders" class="mw-redirect" title="Crusaders">Crusaders</a> mentioned the city as <i>Prineople</i>, <i>Sinople</i> and <i>Phinepople</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-pld_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pld-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The Ottomans called the city <i>Filibe</i>, a corruption of "Philip", in a document from 1448.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_Bulgaria_by_Sentinel-2_20190608.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Plovdiv_Bulgaria_by_Sentinel-2_20190608.jpg/220px-Plovdiv_Bulgaria_by_Sentinel-2_20190608.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Plovdiv_Bulgaria_by_Sentinel-2_20190608.jpg/330px-Plovdiv_Bulgaria_by_Sentinel-2_20190608.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Plovdiv_Bulgaria_by_Sentinel-2_20190608.jpg/440px-Plovdiv_Bulgaria_by_Sentinel-2_20190608.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2670" data-file-height="3029" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_Bulgaria_by_Sentinel-2_20190608.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plovdiv seen from space</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B5.jpg/200px-%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B5.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B5.jpg/300px-%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B5.jpg/400px-%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4870" data-file-height="2947" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%B5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view around the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Maritsa" title="Maritsa">Maritsa</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_balkan-1-.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Plovdiv_balkan-1-.jpg/200px-Plovdiv_balkan-1-.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Plovdiv_balkan-1-.jpg/300px-Plovdiv_balkan-1-.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Plovdiv_balkan-1-.jpg/400px-Plovdiv_balkan-1-.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_balkan-1-.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of Plovdiv with the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Mountains" title="Balkan Mountains">Balkan Mountains</a> in the background.</div></div></div>\n<p>Plovdiv is located on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Maritsa" title="Maritsa">Maritsa</a> river, southeast of the Bulgarian capital <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>. The city is in the southern part of the <i>Plain of Plovdiv</i>, an <a href="/wiki/Alluvial_plain" title="Alluvial plain">alluvial plain</a> that forms the western portion of the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Thracian_Plain" title="Upper Thracian Plain">Upper Thracian Plain</a>. From there, the peaks of the <a href="/wiki/Sredna_Gora" title="Sredna Gora">Sredna Gora</a> mountain range rise to the northwest, the Chirpan Heights to the east, and the <a href="/wiki/Rhodope_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhodope mountains">Rhodope mountains</a> to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Originally, Plovdiv\'s development occurred south of Maritsa, with expansion across the river taking place only within the last 100 years. Modern Plovdiv covers an area of 101&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (39&#160;sq&#160;mi), less than 0.1% of Bulgaria\'s total area. It is the most densely populated city in Bulgaria, with 3,769 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>.\n</p><p>Inside the city proper are six <a href="/wiki/Syenite" title="Syenite">syenite</a> hills. At the beginning of the 20th century, there were seven syenite hills, but one (<a href="/wiki/Markovo_tepe" class="mw-redirect" title="Markovo tepe">Markovo tepe</a>) was destroyed. Three of them are called the Three Hills (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">\xd0\xa2\xd1\x80\xd0\xb8\xd1\x85\xd1\x8a\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbc\xd0\xb8\xd0\xb5</span> <i>Trihalmie</i>), the others are called the Hill of the Youth (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">\xd0\x9c\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb4\xd0\xb5\xd0\xb6\xd0\xba\xd0\xb8 \xd1\x85\xd1\x8a\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbc</span>, <i>Mladezhki halm</i>), the Hill of the Liberators (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">\xd0\xa5\xd1\x8a\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbc \xd0\xbd\xd0\xb0 \xd0\xbe\xd1\x81\xd0\xb2\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb1\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb4\xd0\xb8\xd1\x82\xd0\xb5\xd0\xbb\xd0\xb8\xd1\x82\xd0\xb5</span>, <i>Halm na osvoboditelite</i>), and the Hill of <a href="/wiki/Hristo_G._Danov" title="Hristo G. Danov">Danov</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">\xd0\x94\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbd\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2 \xd1\x85\xd1\x8a\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbc</span>, <i>Danov halm</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Plovdiv has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a> <i>Cfa</i>) with considerable <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental" class="mw-redirect" title="Humid continental">humid continental</a> influences. There are four distinct seasons with large temperature jumps between seasons.\n</p><p>Summer (mid-May to late September) is hot, moderately dry and sunny, with July and August having an average high of 33&#160;\xc2\xb0C (91&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Plovdiv sometimes experiences very hot days which are typical in the interior of the country. Summer nights are mild.\n</p><p>Autumn starts in late September; days are long and relatively warm in early autumn. The nights become chilly by September. The first frost usually occurs by November.\n</p><p>Winter is normally cold and snow is common. The average number of days with snow coverage in Plovdiv is 15. The average depth of snow coverage is 2 to 4&#160;cm (1 to 2&#160;in), and the maximum is normally 6 to 13&#160;cm (2 to 5&#160;in), but some winters coverage can reach 70&#160;cm (28&#160;in) or more. The average January temperature is \xe2\x88\x920.4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (31&#160;\xc2\xb0F).\n</p><p>Spring begins in March and is cooler than autumn. The frost season ends in March. The days are mild and relatively warm in mid-spring.\n</p><p>The average relative humidity is 73% and is highest in December at 86% and the lowest in August at 62%. The total precipitation is 540&#160;mm (21.26&#160;in) and is fairly evenly distributed throughout the year. The wettest months of the year are May and June, with an average precipitation of 66.2&#160;mm (2.61&#160;in), and the driest month is August, with an average precipitation of 31&#160;mm (1.22&#160;in).\n</p><p>Gentle winds (0 to 5&#160;m/s) are predominant in the city with wind speeds of up to 1&#160;m/s, representing 95% of all winds during the year. Mists are common in the cooler months, especially along the banks of the Maritsa. On average there are 33&#160;days with <a href="/wiki/Mist" title="Mist">mist</a> during the year.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:100%; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">9.2<br />(48.6)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: [Stringmeteo.com]\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Philippopolis_(Thracia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippopolis (Thracia)">Philippopolis (Thracia)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Plovdiv" title="Timeline of Plovdiv">Timeline of Plovdiv</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Plovdiv" title="History of Plovdiv">History of Plovdiv</a></div>\n<table border="1" cellpadding="4" cellspacing="0" style="float:right;
