class="sidebar-content">\n&#160;&#8226;&#32;<a href="/wiki/History_of_Plovdiv" title="History of Plovdiv">History</a>&#160;&#8226;&#32;<a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Plovdiv" title="Timeline of Plovdiv">Timeline</a></td>\n</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar" style="text-align:center;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Philippopolis_sidebar" title="Template:Philippopolis sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Philippopolis_sidebar" title="Template talk:Philippopolis sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Philippopolis_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The history of Plovdiv spans more than eight millennia. Numerous nations have left their traces on the twelve-metre-thick (39-<a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">foot</a>) cultural layers of the city. The earliest signs of habitation in the territory of Plovdiv date as far back as the 6th millennium BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-filipopol_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filipopol-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-plovdiv1_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plovdiv1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Plovdiv has settlement traces including necropolises dating from the Neolithic era (roughly 6000\xe2\x80\x935000 BCE) like the mounds Yasa Tepe 1 in the Philipovo district and Yasa Tepe 2 in Lauta park.<sup id="cite_ref-\xd1\x80\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb9\xd1\x87\xd0\xb5\xd0\xb2\xd1\x81\xd0\xba\xd0\xb8_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-\xd1\x80\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb9\xd1\x87\xd0\xb5\xd0\xb2\xd1\x81\xd0\xba\xd0\xb8-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-\xd0\xba\xd0\xb5\xd1\x81\xd1\x8f\xd0\xba\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb0_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-\xd0\xba\xd0\xb5\xd1\x81\xd1\x8f\xd0\xba\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb2\xd0\xb0-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Archaeologists have discovered fine pottery<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and objects of everyday life on <a href="/wiki/Nebet_Tepe" title="Nebet Tepe">Nebet Tepe</a> from as early as the <a href="/wiki/Chalcolithic" title="Chalcolithic">Chalcolithic</a> era, showing that at the end of the 4th millennium BCE, there was already an established settlement there which was <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_continuously_inhabited_cities" title="List of oldest continuously inhabited cities">continuously inhabited</a> since then.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Thracian necropolises dating back to the 2nd\xe2\x80\x933rd millennium BCE have been discovered, while the Thracian town was established between the 2nd and the 1st millennium BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The town was a fort of the independent local <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a> tribe <a href="/wiki/Bessi" title="Bessi">Bessi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In 516 BCE during the rule of <a href="/wiki/Darius_the_Great" title="Darius the Great">Darius the Great</a>, Thrace was included in the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Persian empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In 492 BCE, the Persian general <a href="/wiki/Mardonius_(general)" title="Mardonius (general)">Mardonius</a> subjugated Thrace again, and it nominally became a vassal of Persia until 479 BCE and the early rule of <a href="/wiki/Xerxes_I" title="Xerxes I">Xerxes I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The town became part of the <a href="/wiki/Odrysian_kingdom" title="Odrysian kingdom">Odrysian kingdom</a> (460 BCE \xe2\x80\x93 46 CE), a <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracian</a> tribal union. The town was conquered by <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Macedon" title="Philip II of Macedon">Philip II of Macedon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and the Odrysian king was deposed in 342 BCE. Ten years after the Macedonian invasion, the Thracian kings started to exercise power again after the Odrysian <a href="/wiki/Seuthes_III" title="Seuthes III">Seuthes III</a> had re-established their kingdom under Macedonian suzerainty as a result of a successful revolt against <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a>\'s rule resulting in a stalemate.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The Odrysian kingdom gradually overcame the Macedonian suzerainty, while the city was destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_settlement_of_Eastern_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Celtic settlement of Eastern Europe">Celtic settlement of Eastern Europe</a>, most likely in the 270s BC.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In 183 BCE, <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Macedon" title="Philip V of Macedon">Philip V of Macedon</a> conquered the city, but shortly after, the Thracians re-conquered it.\n</p><p>In 72 BCE, the city was seized by the Roman general <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Terentius_Varro_Lucullus" title="Marcus Terentius Varro Lucullus">Marcus Lucullus</a> but was soon restored to Thracian control. In 46 CE, the city was finally incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> by emperor <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">Claudius</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> it served as the capital of the province of <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a> and gained city status in the late 1st century.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Trimontium was an important crossroad for the Roman Empire and was called "the largest and most beautiful of all cities" by <a href="/wiki/Lucian" title="Lucian">Lucian</a>. Although it was not the capital of the Province of Thrace, the city was the largest and most important centre in the province.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> As such, the city was the seat of the Union of Thracians.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In those times, the <a href="/wiki/Via_Militaris" title="Via Militaris">Via Militaris</a> (or Via Diagonalis), the most important military road in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, passed through the city.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The Roman times were a period of growth and cultural excellence.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The ancient ruins tell a story of a vibrant, growing city with numerous public buildings, shrines, baths, theatres, a stadium, and the only developed ancient water supply system in Bulgaria. The city had an advanced water system and <a href="/wiki/Sanitary_sewer" title="Sanitary sewer">sewerage</a>. In 179 a second wall was built to encompass Trimontium which had already extended out of the Three hills into the valley. Many of those are still preserved and can be seen by tourists. Today only a small part of the ancient city has been excavated.<sup id="cite_ref-pldiv_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pldiv-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 250 the city was captured and looted after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Philippopolis_(250)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Philippopolis (250)">Battle of Philippopolis</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>, led by their ruler <a href="/wiki/Cniva" title="Cniva">Cniva</a>. Many of its citizens, 100,000 according to <a href="/wiki/Ammianus_Marcellinus" title="Ammianus Marcellinus">Ammianus Marcellinus</a>, died or were taken captive.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> It took a century and hard work to recover the city. However, it was destroyed again by <a href="/wiki/Attila" title="Attila">Attila</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Hun" class="mw-redirect" title="Hun">Huns</a> in 441\xe2\x80\x93442 and by the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a> of Teodoric Strabo in 471.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An ancient Roman inscription written in Ancient Greek dated to 253 \xe2\x80\x93 255 AD were discovered in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Basilica,_Plovdiv" title="Great Basilica, Plovdiv">Great Basilica</a>. The inscription refers to the <a href="/wiki/Dionysian_Mysteries" title="Dionysian Mysteries">Dionysian Mysteries</a> and also mentions Roman Emperors <a href="/wiki/Valerian_(emperor)" title="Valerian (emperor)">Valerian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gallienus" title="Gallienus">Gallienus</a>. It has been found on a large stele which was used as construction material during the building of the Great Basilica.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Monument_of_Khan_Krum_in_Plovdiv.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Monument_of_Khan_Krum_in_Plovdiv.jpg/220px-Monument_of_Khan_Krum_in_Plovdiv.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Monument_of_Khan_Krum_in_Plovdiv.jpg/330px-Monument_of_Khan_Krum_in_Plovdiv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Monument_of_Khan_Krum_in_Plovdiv.jpg/440px-Monument_of_Khan_Krum_in_Plovdiv.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="1584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Monument_of_Khan_Krum_in_Plovdiv.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument of <a href="/wiki/Krum_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Krum of Bulgaria">Krum</a> in Plovdiv, who was the first Bulgarian ruler to capture Plovdiv.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic peoples">The Slavs</a> had fully settled in the area by the middle of the 6th century. This was done peacefully as there are no records for their attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>  With the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> in 681, Philippoupolis, the name of the city then, became an important border fortress of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>. It was captured by Khan <a href="/wiki/Krum_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Krum of Bulgaria">Krum</a> in 812, but the region was fully incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian Empire</a> in 834 during the reign of Khan <a href="/wiki/Malamir_of_Bulgaria" title="Malamir of Bulgaria">Malamir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> It was reconquered by the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> in 855\xe2\x80\x93856 for a short time until it was returned to <a href="/wiki/Boris_I_of_Bulgaria" title="Boris I of Bulgaria">Boris I of Bulgaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> From Philippopolis, the influence of <a href="/wiki/Dualistic_cosmology" class="mw-redirect" title="Dualistic cosmology">dualistic</a> doctrines spread to Bulgaria forming the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Bogomil" class="mw-redirect" title="Bogomil">Bogomil</a> heresy. The city remained in Bulgarian hands until 970.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> However, the city is described at the time of <a href="/wiki/Constantine_VII" title="Constantine VII">Constantine VII</a> in the 10th century as being within the Byzantine province (<a href="/wiki/Theme_(Byzantine_district)" title="Theme (Byzantine district)">theme</a> of <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(theme)" title="Macedonia (theme)">Macedonia</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Philippopolis was captured by the Byzantines in 969, shortly before it was sacked by the ruler of <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus&#39;">Rus\'</a> <a href="/wiki/Sviatoslav_I_of_Kiev" class="mw-redirect" title="Sviatoslav I of Kiev">Sviatoslav I of Kiev</a> who impaled 20,000 citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Before and after the Rus\' massacre, the city was settled by <a href="/wiki/Paulician" class="mw-redirect" title="Paulician">Paulician</a> heretics transported from Syria and Armenia to serve as military settlers on the European frontier with Bulgaria. Aime de Varennes in 1180 encountered the singing of Byzantine songs in the city that recounted the deeds of Alexander the Great and his predecessors over 1300 years before.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Byzantine rule was interrupted by the <a href="/wiki/Third_crusade" class="mw-redirect" title="Third crusade">Third crusade</a> (1189\xe2\x80\x931192) when the army of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman</a> emperor <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Barbarossa" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick Barbarossa">Frederick Barbarossa</a> conquered Philippopolis. <a href="/wiki/Ivanko_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivanko of Bulgaria">Ivanko</a> was appointed as the governor of the Byzantine Theme of Philippopolis in 1196, but between 1198 and 1200 separated it from Byzantium in a union with Bulgaria. The <a href="/wiki/Latin_Empire" title="Latin Empire">Latin Empire</a> conquered Philippoupolis in 1204, and there were two short interregnum periods as the city was twice occupied by <a href="/wiki/Kaloyan_of_Bulgaria" title="Kaloyan of Bulgaria">Kaloyan of Bulgaria</a> before his death in 1207.<sup id="cite_ref-pldv_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pldv-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In 1208, Kaloyan\'s successor <a href="/wiki/Boril_of_Bulgaria" title="Boril of Bulgaria">Boril</a> was defeated by the Latins in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Philippopolis_(1208)" title="Battle of Philippopolis (1208)">Battle of Philippopolis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Under Latin rule, Philippopolis was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Philippopolis" title="Duchy of Philippopolis">Duchy of Philippopolis</a>, which was governed by <a href="/wiki/Renier_de_Trit" class="mw-redirect" title="Renier de Trit">Renier de Trit</a> and later on by Gerard de Strem. The city was possibly at times a vassal of Bulgaria or <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Asen_II_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivan Asen II of Bulgaria">Ivan Asen II</a> conquered the duchy finally in 1230 but the city had possibly been conquered earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Afterwards, Philippopolis was conquered by Byzantium. According to some information, by 1300 Philippopolis was a possession of <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Svetoslav" class="mw-redirect" title="Theodore Svetoslav">Theodore Svetoslav</a> of Bulgaria. It was conquered from Byzantium by <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Bulgaria" title="George II of Bulgaria">George Terter II</a> of Bulgaria in 1322.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andronikos_III_Palaiologos" title="Andronikos III Palaiologos">Andronikos III Palaiologos</a> unsuccessfully besieged the city, but a treaty restored Byzantine rule once again in 1323. In 1344 the city and eight other cities were surrendered to Bulgaria by the regency for <a href="/wiki/John_V_Palaiologos" title="John V Palaiologos">John V Palaiologos</a> as the price for <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Alexander_of_Bulgaria" title="Ivan Alexander of Bulgaria">Ivan Alexander of Bulgaria</a>\'s support in the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_civil_war_of_1341%E2%80%9347" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine civil war of 1341\xe2\x80\x9347">Byzantine civil war of 1341\xe2\x80\x9347</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_rule">Ottoman rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ottoman rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1364 the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a> under <a href="/wiki/Lala_Shahin_Pasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Lala Shahin Pasha">Lala Shahin Pasha</a> seized Plovdiv.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pat_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pat-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> According to other data, Plovdiv was not an Ottoman possession until the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Maritsa" title="Battle of Maritsa">Battle of Maritsa</a> in 1371, after which, the citizens and the Bulgarian army fled leaving the city without resistance. Refugees settled in <a href="/wiki/Asenovgrad" title="Asenovgrad">Stanimaka</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Interregnum" title="Ottoman Interregnum">Ottoman Interregnum</a> in 1410, <a href="/wiki/Musa_%C3%87elebi" title="Musa \xc3\x87elebi">Musa \xc3\x87elebi</a> conquered the city killing and displacing inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-egeweb2.ege.edu.tr_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-egeweb2.ege.edu.tr-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The city was the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Rumelia_Eyalet" title="Rumelia Eyalet">Rumelia Eyalet</a> from 1364 until 1443, when it was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> as the capital of <a href="/wiki/Rumelia" title="Rumelia">Rumelia</a>. Plovdiv served as a sanjak centre within Rumelia between 1443 and 1593, the sanjak centre in <a href="/wiki/Silistra_Eyalet" title="Silistra Eyalet">Silistra Eyalet</a> between 1593 and 1826, the sanjak centre in <a href="/wiki/Eyalet_of_Adrianople" title="Eyalet of Adrianople">Eyalet of Adrianople</a> between 1826 and 1867, and the sanjak centre of <a href="/wiki/Edirne_Vilayet" class="mw-redirect" title="Edirne Vilayet">Edirne Vilayet</a> between 1867 and 1878. During that period, Plovdiv was one of the major economic centers in the Balkans, along with <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> (<a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>), <a href="/wiki/Edirne" title="Edirne">Edirne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, and Sofia.  The richer citizens constructed beautiful houses, many of which can still be seen in the architectural reserve of Old Plovdiv. From the early 15th century till the end of 17th century the city was predominantly inhabited by Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National_revival">National revival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: National revival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Revival" title="Bulgarian National Revival">Bulgarian National Revival</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Bogoroditza_plovdiv.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/St._Bogoroditza_plovdiv.jpg/200px-St._Bogoroditza_plovdiv.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/St._Bogoroditza_plovdiv.jpg/300px-St._Bogoroditza_plovdiv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/36/St._Bogoroditza_plovdiv.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Bogoroditza_plovdiv.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Mother_of_God,_Plovdiv" title="Church of the Holy Mother of God, Plovdiv">Virgin Mary Church</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, Filibe (as the city was known at that time) was a focal point for the Bulgarian national movement and survived as one of the major cultural centers for Bulgarian culture and tradition.\n</p><p>Filibe was described as consisting of Turks, Bulgarians, Hellenized Bulgarians, Armenians, Jews, Vlachs, Arvanites, Greeks, and Roma people. In the 16\xe2\x80\x9317 century a significant number of <a href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic Jews">Sephardic Jews</a> settled along with a smaller Armenian community from <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)" title="Galicia (Eastern Europe)">Galicia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Paulician" class="mw-redirect" title="Paulician">Paulicians</a> adopted Catholicism or lost their identity. The abolition of <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Slavonic</a> as the language of the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Ohrid" title="Archbishop of Ohrid">Bulgarian Church</a> as well as the complete abolition of the church in 1767 and the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Millet_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Millet (Ottoman Empire)">Millet System</a> led to ethnic division among people of different religions. Christian and Muslim Bulgarians were subjected to <a href="/wiki/Hellenization" title="Hellenization">Hellenization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkification" title="Turkification">Turkification</a> respectively. A major part of the inhabitants was fully or partly Hellenized due to the Greek patriarchate. The "Langeris" are described as Greeks from the area of the nearby <a href="/wiki/Asenovgrad" title="Asenovgrad">Stenimachos</a>. The process of Hellenization flourished until the 1830s but declined with the <a href="/wiki/Tanzimat" title="Tanzimat">Tanzimat</a> as the idea of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Greece_(Wittelsbach)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Greece (Wittelsbach)">Hellenic nation</a> of Christians grew and was associated with ethnic Greeks.\n</p><p>The re-establishment of the Bulgarian Church in 1870 was a sign of ethnic and national consciousness. Thus, although there is a little doubt about the Bulgarian origin of the Gulidas, the city could be considered of Greek or Bulgarian majority in the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Raymond Detrez has suggested that when the Gudilas and Langeris claimed to be Greek it was more in the sense of "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Byzantine_Greels&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Byzantine Greels (page does not exist)">Romei</a> than Ellines, in a cultural rather than an ethnic sense".<sup id="cite_ref-balkanologie_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balkanologie-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> According to the statistics by the Bulgarian and Greek authors, there were no Turks in the city; according to an alternative estimate the city was of Turkish majority.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Filibe had an important role in the struggle for Church independence which was, according to some historians, a peaceful bourgeois revolution. Filibe became the center of that struggle with leaders such as <a href="/wiki/Nayden_Gerov" title="Nayden Gerov">Nayden Gerov</a>, Dr Valkovich, <a href="/wiki/Joakim_Gruev" class="mw-redirect" title="Joakim Gruev">Joakim Gruev</a>, and whole families. In 1836 the first Bulgarian school was inaugurated, and in 1850, modern secular education began when the "St Cyrill and Methodius" school was opened. On 11 May 1858, the day of <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">Saints Cyril and Methodius</a> was celebrated for the first time; this later became a National holiday which is still celebrated today (but on 24 May due to Bulgaria\'s 1916 transition from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Style" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Style">Old Style</a> (<a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian</a>) to the <a href="/wiki/Adoption_of_the_Gregorian_calendar#Adoption_in_Eastern_Europe" title="Adoption of the Gregorian calendar">New Style</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian</a>) calendar). In 1858 in the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Mother_of_God,_Plovdiv" title="Church of the Holy Mother of God, Plovdiv">Church of Virgin Mary</a>, the Christmas liturgy was served for the first time in the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian language</a> since the beginning of the Ottoman occupation. Until 1906 there were Bulgarian and Greek bishops in the city. In 1868 the school expanded into the first grammar school. Some of the intellectuals, politicians, and spiritual leaders of the nation graduated that school.<sup id="cite_ref-pld_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pld-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city was conquered by the Russians under <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Burago" title="Aleksandr Burago">Aleksandr Burago</a> for several hours during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Philippopolis_(1878)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Philippopolis (1878)">Battle of Philippopolis</a> on 17 January 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-pat_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pat-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> It was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Russian_Administration_in_Bulgaria" title="Provisional Russian Administration in Bulgaria">Provisional Russian Administration in Bulgaria</a> between May and October. According to the Russian census of the same year, Filibe had a population of 24,000 citizens, of which ethnic <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a> comprised 45.4%, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a> 23.1% and <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> 19.9%.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Rumelia">Eastern Rumelia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Eastern Rumelia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_unification" title="Bulgarian unification">Bulgarian unification</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_3.jpg/220px-Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_3.jpg/330px-Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_3.jpg/440px-Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="702" data-file-height="653" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nebet Tepe, drawing from The Graphic \xe2\x80\x93 London, 1885</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_1.jpg/220px-Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_1.jpg/330px-Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_1.jpg/440px-Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="699" data-file-height="659" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_1885_the_graphic_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Taat tepe, in Plovdiv, with the governor\'s palace and Maritsa river in the foreground. Drawing from The Graphic \xe2\x80\x93 London, 1885</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Stefano" title="Treaty of San Stefano">Treaty of San Stefano</a> on 3 March 1878, the Principality of Bulgaria included the lands with predominantly Bulgarian population. Plovdiv which was the biggest and most vibrant Bulgarian city was selected as a capital of the restored country and for a seat of the Temporary Russian Government.<sup id="cite_ref-ocertsi_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocertsi-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Great Britain and <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, however, did not approve that treaty and the final result of the war was concluded in the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">Congress of Berlin</a> which divided the newly liberated country into several parts. It separated the autonomous region of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Rumelia" title="Eastern Rumelia">Eastern Rumelia</a> from Bulgaria, and Plovdiv became its capital. The Ottoman Empire created a constitution and appointed a governor.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the spring of 1885, <a href="/wiki/Zahari_Stoyanov" title="Zahari Stoyanov">Zahari Stoyanov</a> formed the Secret Bulgarian Central Revolutionary Committee in the city which actively conducted propaganda for the unification of Bulgaria and Eastern Rumelia. On 5 September, several hundred armed rebels from Golyamo Konare (now <a href="/wiki/Saedinenie,_Plovdiv_Province" title="Saedinenie, Plovdiv Province">Saedinenie</a>) marched to Plovdiv. In the night of 5\xe2\x80\x936 September, these men, led by Danail Nikolaev, took control of the city and removed from office the General-Governor <a href="/wiki/Gavril_Krastevich" title="Gavril Krastevich">Gavril Krastevich</a>. A provisional government was formed led by <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Stranski" title="Georgi Stranski">Georgi Stranski</a>, and universal mobilization was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> After the Serbs were defeated in the <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Bulgarian_War" title="Serbo-Bulgarian War">Serbo-Bulgarian War</a>, Bulgaria and Turkey reached an agreement that the Principality of Bulgaria and Eastern Rumelia had a common government, Parliament, administration, and army. Today, 6 September is celebrated as the Unification Day and the Day of Plovdiv.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After the unification, Plovdiv remained the second most populous city in Bulgaria after the capital <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>. The first railway in the city was built in 1874 connecting it with the Ottoman capital, and in 1888, it was linked with Sofia. In 1892 Plovdiv became the host of the First Bulgarian Fair with international participation which was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/International_Fair_Plovdiv" title="International Fair Plovdiv">International Fair Plovdiv</a>. After the liberation, the first brewery was inaugurated in the city.\n</p><p>In the beginning of the 20th century, Plovdiv grew as a significant industrial and commercial center with well-developed light and food industry. In 1927 the electrification of Plovdiv has started. German, French, and <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgian</a> capital was invested in the city in the development of modern trade, banking, and industry. In 1939 there were 16,000 craftsmen and 17,000 workers in manufacturing factories, mainly for food and tobacco processing. During the Second World War, the tobacco industry expanded as well as the export of fruit and vegetables. In 1943, 1,500 Jews were saved from deportation in <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp">concentration camps</a> by the archbishop of Plovdiv, <a href="/wiki/Patriarch_Cyril_of_Bulgaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Patriarch Cyril of Bulgaria">Cyril</a>, who later became the Bulgarian Patriarch. In 1944 the city was bombed by the British-American coalition.\n</p><p>Tobacco Depot workers went on strike on 4 May 1953.\n</p><p>On 6 April 1956 the first trolleybus line was opened and in the 1950s the Trimontsium Hotel was constructed. In the 1960s and 1970s, there was a construction boom and many of the modern neighborhoods took shape. In the 1970s and 1980s, antique remains were excavated and the Old Town was fully restored. In 1990 the sports complex "Plovdiv" was finished. It included the largest stadium and rowing canal in the country. In that period, Plovdiv became the birthplace of Bulgaria\'s movement for democratic reform, which by 1989 had garnered enough support to enter government.\n</p><p>Plovdiv has hosted specialized exhibitions of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s Fair">World\'s Fair</a> in 1981, 1985, and 1991.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1608px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Plovdiv_panorama.jpg/1600px-Plovdiv_panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="1600" height="337" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Plovdiv_panorama.jpg/2400px-Plovdiv_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Plovdiv_panorama.jpg/3200px-Plovdiv_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8368" data-file-height="1760" /></a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1608px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdivpanorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Plovdivpanorama.jpg/1600px-Plovdivpanorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="1600" height="249" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Plovdivpanorama.jpg/2400px-Plovdivpanorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Plovdivpanorama.jpg/3200px-Plovdivpanorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4501" data-file-height="700" /></a></div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The population by permanent address for the municipality of Plovdiv for 2007 is 380,682,<sup id="cite_ref-grao.bg_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grao.bg-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> which makes it the second in population in the nation. According to data from the National Institute of Statistics (NSI), the population of people who actually live in Plovdiv is 346,790.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\nAccording to the 2012 census, 339,077 live within the city limits and 403,153 in the municipal triangle of Plovdiv, including <a href="/wiki/Maritsa_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritsa municipality">Maritsa municipality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rodopi_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Rodopi municipality">Rodopi municipality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-census_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\nPopulation of Plovdiv:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" width="750px" style="font-size: 93%; As of the 1887 census, Plovdiv was the largest city in the country for several years with 33,032 inhabitants compared to 30,428 for Sofia. According to the 1946 census, Plovdiv was the second largest city with 126,563 inhabitants compared to 487,000 for the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-ocertsi_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocertsi-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity_and_religion">Ethnicity and religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span (1.36%)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>2001<sup id="cite_ref-mncp_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mncp-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7005338224000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>338<span style="margin-left:.25em;">224</span></span></td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7004225010000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>22<span style="margin-left:.25em;">501</span></span> (6.7%)</td>\n<td></td>\n<td></td>\n<td></td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003519200000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>5192</span> (1.5%)</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003576400000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>5764</span> (1.7%)</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003190900000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>1909</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>2011<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7005338153000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>338<span style="margin-left:.25em;">153</span></span></td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7005277804000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>277<span style="margin-left:.25em;">804</span></span> (82.2%)</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7004160320000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>16<span style="margin-left:.25em;">032</span></span> (4.7%)</td>\n<td></td>\n<td></td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003943800000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>9438</span> (2.8%)</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003143600000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>1436</span> (0.4%)</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003310500000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>3105</span> (0.9%)</td>\n<td><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7004317740000000000\xe2\x99\xa0"></span>31<span style="margin-left:.25em;">774</span></span> (9.4%)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In its ethnic character Plovdiv is the second or the third-largest cosmopolitan city inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> and possibly <a href="/wiki/Varna,_Bulgaria" title="Varna, Bulgaria">Varna</a>. According to the 2001 census, out of a population of 338,224 inhabitants, the Bulgarians numbered 302,858 (90%). <a href="/wiki/Stolipinovo" title="Stolipinovo">Stolipinovo</a> in Plovdiv is the largest Roma neighbourhood in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, having a population of around 20,000 alone; further Roma ghettos are <a href="/wiki/Hadji_Hassan_Mahala" title="Hadji Hassan Mahala">Hadji Hassan Mahala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheker_Mahala" title="Sheker Mahala">Sheker Mahala</a>. Therefore, the census number is a deflation of the number of Roma people, and they are most likely the second-largest group after the Bulgarians, most of all because the Muslim Roma in Plovdiv claim to be of Turkish ethnicity and Turkish-speaking at the census ("<a href="/wiki/Xoraxane" class="mw-redirect" title="Xoraxane">Xoraxane</a> Roma").<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> For further information see the article <a href="/wiki/The_Roma_in_Plovdiv" class="mw-redirect" title="The Roma in Plovdiv">Roma people in Plovdiv</a>. Like elsewhere in the country, Roma people are subjected to discrimination and segregation (See the Bulgaria section of the article <a href="/wiki/Antiziganism" title="Antiziganism">Antiziganism</a>).\n</p><p>After the Wars for National Union (<a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> and World War I), the city became home for thousands of refugees from the former Bulgarian lands in <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Thrace" title="Western Thrace">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Thrace" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Thrace">Eastern Thrace</a>. Many of the old neighbourhoods are still referred to as <i>Belomorski</i>, <i>Vardarski</i>. Most of the Jews left the city after the foundation of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> in 1948, as well as most of the Turks and Greeks. Prior to the population exchange, as of 1 January 1885, the city of Plovdiv had a population of 33,442, of which 16,752 were <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a> (50%), 7,144 <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a> (21%), 5,497 <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> (16%), 2,168 Jews (6%), 1,061 <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a> (3%), 151 <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italians</a>, 112 <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, 112 <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a>, 80 <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French people</a>, 61 <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> and 304 people of other nationalities.<sup id="cite_ref-histmuseum_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-histmuseum-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The vast majority of the inhabitants are Christians, mostly <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a>, Catholics, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Catholic">Eastern Catholics</a>, and Protestant trends (<a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Adventists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> and others). There are also some <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> and Jews. In Plovdiv, there are many churches, two mosques and one synagogue (see <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Synagogue" title="Plovdiv Synagogue">Plovdiv Synagogue</a>).\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>The Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="City_government">City government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: City government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Plovdiv is the administrative center of <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Province" title="Plovdiv Province">Plovdiv Province</a> which consists of the Municipality of Plovdiv, the <a href="/wiki/Maritsa_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritsa municipality">Maritsa municipality</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Rodopi_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Rodopi municipality">Rodopi municipality</a>. The mayor of the Municipality of Plovdiv, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ivan_Totev&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ivan Totev (page does not exist)">Ivan Totev</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> with the six district mayors represent the local executive authorities. The Municipal Council which consists of 51 municipal counsellors, represents the legislative power, and is elected according to the proportional system by parties\' lists.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The executive government of the Municipality of Plovdiv consists of a mayor who is elected by majority representation, five deputy mayors, and one administrative secretary. All the deputy mayors and the secretary control their administrative structured units.\n</p><p>According to the <i>Law for the territorial subdivision of the Capital municipality and the large cities,</i><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> the territory of Plovdiv Municipality is subdivided into six district administrations with their mayors being appointed following approval by the Municipal Council.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts_and_neighbourhoods">Districts and neighbourhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Districts and neighbourhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="img" class="noresize" style="width: 500px; padding: 5px; line-height: 1; text-align: center; background-color: #ffffff; position: top:368px">18</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:178px; top:340px">19</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:190px; top:280px">20</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:94px; top:324px">24</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:154px; top:244px">25</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:146px; top:220px">26</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:198px; top:164px">30</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:262px; top:148px">31</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:234px; top:104px">32</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:198px; top:140px">33</div>\n<div style="position:absolute; left:158px; top:148px">34</div>\n</div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Number\n</th>\n<th>Neighbourhood\n</th>\n<th>Number\n</th>\n<th>Neighbourhood\n</th>\n<th>Number\n</th>\n<th>Neighbourhood\n</th>\n<th>Number\n</th>\n<th>Neighbourhood\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>Center\n</td>\n<td>12</td>\n<td>Sadiiski\n</td>\n<td>23</td>\n<td>Hristo Gara\n</td>\n<td>24</td>\n<td>Proslav\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>3</td>\n<td>Kamenitsa 1\n</td>\n<td>14</td>\n<td>Kyutchuk Paris\n</td>\n<td>25</td>\n<td>Mladezhki Halm\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>4</td>\n<td>Kamenitsa 2\n</td>\n<td>15</td>\n<td>Vastannicheski\n</td>\n<td>26</td>\n<td>Otdih i Kultura\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>Izgrev\n</td>\n<td>16</td>\n<td>Belomorski\n</td>\n<td>27</td>\n<td>Marasha\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>6</td>\n<td>Stolipinovo\n</td>\n<td>17</td>\n<td>Institut po Ovoshtarstvo\n</td>\n<td>28</td>\n<td>Maritsa Sever\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>7</td>\n<td>Izgrev\n</td>\n<td>18</td>\n<td>Ostromila\n</td>\n<td>29</td>\n<td>Zaharna Fabrika\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>8</td>\n<td>Industrial zone \xe2\x80\x93 East\n</td>\n<td>19</td>\n<td>Yuzhen\n</td>\n<td>30</td>\n<td>Karshiaka\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>9</td>\n<td>Trakia\n</td>\n<td>20</td>\n<td>Tsentralna Gara\n</td>\n<td>31</td>\n<td>Gagarin\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>10</td>\n<td>Industrial zone \xe2\x80\x93 Trakia\n</td>\n<td>21</td>\n<td>Komatevo\n</td>\n<td>32</td>\n<td>Industrial Zone \xe2\x80\x93 North\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>11</td>\n<td>Industrial zone \xe2\x80\x93 South\n</td>\n<td>22</td>\n<td>Komatevski Vazel\n</td>\n<td>33</td>\n<td>Filipovo\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>In 1969 the villages of <a href="/wiki/Proslav" title="Proslav">Proslav</a> and <a href="/wiki/Komatevo" title="Komatevo">Komatevo</a> were incorporated into the city. In 1987 the municipalities of Maritsa and Rodopi were separated from Plovdiv which remained their administrative center. In the last several years, the inhabitants from those villages had taken steps to rejoin the "urban" municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The city has more than 200 archaeological sites,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> 30 of which are of national importance. There are many remains from antiquity. Plovdiv is among the few cities with two ancient theatres; remains of the medieval walls and towers; Ottoman baths and mosques; a well-preserved old quarter from the National Revival period with beautiful houses; churches; and narrow paved streets. There are numerous museums, art, galleries and cultural institutions. Plovdiv is host to musical, theatrical, and film events. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Knyaz_Alexander_I_Street&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Knyaz Alexander I Street (page does not exist)">Knyaz Alexander I Street</a> is the main street in Plovdiv.\n</p><p>The city is a starting point for trips to places in the region, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bachkovo_Monastery" title="Bachkovo Monastery">Bachkovo Monastery</a> at 30&#160;km (19&#160;mi) to the south, the ski-resort <a href="/wiki/Pamporovo" title="Pamporovo">Pamporovo</a> at 90&#160;km (56&#160;mi) to the south or the <a href="/wiki/Spa_resort" class="mw-redirect" title="Spa resort">spa resorts</a> to the north <a href="/wiki/Hisarya" class="mw-redirect" title="Hisarya">Hisarya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banya,_Plovdiv_Province" title="Banya, Plovdiv Province">Banya</a>, Krasnovo, and <a href="/wiki/Strelcha" title="Strelcha">Strelcha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_City">Roman City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Roman City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r997900035"/><div class="locmap noviewer thumb tright"><div //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Museum_black_icon.svg/30px-Museum_black_icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></div><div class="pl" style="font-size:70%;width:6em;right:9px"><div><a href="/wiki/Eirene_Residence_(Plovdiv)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eirene Residence (Plovdiv)">Eirene Residence</a></div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_city_center_map.png" title="File:Plovdiv city center map.png"> </a></div>Ancient monuments in Plovdiv</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Roman_theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Plovdiv Roman theatre">Ancient theatre (Antichen teatur)</a> is probably the best-known monument from <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">antiquity</a> in Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> During recent archaeological survey, an inscription was found on a postament of a statue at the theatre. It revealed that the site was constructed at the 90s of the 1st century CE. The inscription itself refers to Titus Flavius Cotis, the ruler of the ancient city during the reign of Emperor Domitian.\n</p><p>The Ancient theatre is situated in the natural saddle between two of the Three Hills. It is divided into two parts with 14 rows each divided with a horizontal lane. The theatre could accommodate up to 7,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The three-story scene is on the southern part and is decorated with <a href="/wiki/Frieze" title="Frieze">friezes</a>, cornices, and statues. The theatre was studied, conserved, and restored between 1968 and 1984. Many events are still held on the scene<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> including the Opera Festival Opera Open, the Rock Festival Sounds of the Ages, and the International Folklore festival. The Roman Odeon was restored in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> It was built in the 2nd\xe2\x80\x935th centuries and is the second (and smaller) antique <a href="/wiki/Odeon_of_Philippopolis" title="Odeon of Philippopolis">theatre of Philipopolis</a> with 350 seats. It was initially built as a bulevterion, an edifice of the city council, and was later reconstructed as a theatre.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Roman_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Plovdiv Roman Stadium">Ancient Stadium</a><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> is another important monument of the ancient city. It was built in the 2nd century during the reign of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> Emperor <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a>. It is situated between Danov Hill and one of the Three Hills, beneath the main street from Dzhumaya Square to Kamenitsa Square. It was modelled after the stadium in <a href="/wiki/Delphi" title="Delphi">Delphi</a>. It was approximately 240 metres (790 feet) long and 50 metres (160 feet) wide, and could seat up to 30,000 spectators. The athletic games at the stadium were organised by the General Assembly of the province of Thrace. In their honour, the royal mint of Philippopolis coined money featuring the face of the ruling emperor as well as the types of athletic events held in the stadium. Only a small part of the northern section with 14 seat rows can be seen today; the larger part lies under the main street and a number of buildings.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Roman_Forum_(Plovdiv)" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Forum (Plovdiv)">The Roman forum</a> dates from the reign of <a href="/wiki/Vespasian" title="Vespasian">Vespasian</a> in the 1st century and was finished in the 2nd century. It is near the modern post office next to the Odeon. It has an area of 11 hectares and was surrounded by shops and public buildings. The forum was a focal point of the streets of the ancient city.<sup id="cite_ref-ppdv_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ppdv-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Eirene_Residence_(Plovdiv)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eirene Residence (Plovdiv)">Eirene Residence</a> is in the southern part of the Three Hills on the northern part of an ancient street in the Archeological underpass. It includes remains of a public building from the 3rd\xe2\x80\x934th centuries which belonged to a noble citizen. Eirene is the Christian name for Penelopa, a maiden from Megadon, who was converted to Christianity in the 2nd century. There are colourful mosaics which have geometrical forms and figures.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On <a href="/wiki/Nebet_Tepe" title="Nebet Tepe">Nebet hill</a> are the remains of the first settlement which in 12th century BC grew to the <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thracian</a> city of Eumolpias, one of the first cities in Southeastern Europe. Massive walls surrounding a temple and a palace have been excavated. The oldest part of the fortress was constructed from large syenite blocks, the so-called "cyclopean construction".\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed-hover center">\n\t<li Tepe</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div></div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_protected_sites">Museums and protected sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Museums and protected sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Archaeological Museum was established in 1882 as the People\'s Museum of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Rumelia" title="Eastern Rumelia">Eastern Rumelia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> In 1928 the museum was moved to a 19th-century edifice on Saedinenie Square built by Plovdiv architect <a href="/wiki/Josef_Schnitter" title="Josef Schnitter">Josef Schnitter</a>. The museum contains a rich collection of Thracian art. The three sections "Prehistory",<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> "Antiquity",<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> and "Middle Ages"<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> contain precious artifacts from the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> to the early Ottoman period (15th\xe2\x80\x9316th centuries).<sup id="cite_ref-mus_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mus-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The famous <a href="/wiki/Panagyurishte_treasure" class="mw-redirect" title="Panagyurishte treasure">Panagyurishte treasure</a> is part of the museum\'s collection.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Regional_Historical_Museum" title="Plovdiv Regional Historical Museum">Plovdiv Regional Historical Museum</a><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> was founded in 1951 as a scientific and cultural institute for collecting, saving, and researching historical evidence about Plovdiv and the surrounding region from 16th to 20th centuries. The exhibition is situated in three buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-mus_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mus-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Regional_Ethnographic_Museum" title="Plovdiv Regional Ethnographic Museum">Plovdiv Regional Ethnographic Museum</a> was inaugurated in 1917. On 14 October 1943, it was moved to a house in the Old Town. In 1949 the Municipal House-museum was reorganized as a People\'s Ethnographic Museum and in 1962 it was renovated. There are more than 40,000 objects.<sup id="cite_ref-mus_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mus-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Museum of Natural Science was inaugurated in 1955 in the old edifice of the Plovdiv Municipality built in 1880. It is among the most important museums in the country with rich collections in its <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">Paleontology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mineralogy" title="Mineralogy">Mineralogy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">Botanic</a> sections. There are several rooms for wildlife and it contains Bulgaria\'s largest freshwater aquarium with 40 fish species.<sup id="cite_ref-mus_117-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mus-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> It has a collection of minerals from the <a href="/wiki/Rhodope_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhodope mountains">Rhodope mountains</a>.\n</p><p>The Museum of Aviation was established on 21 September 1991 on the territory of the Krumovo airbase<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> 12&#160;km (7&#160;mi) to the southeast of the city. The museum possesses 59 aircraft and indoor and outdoor exhibitions.<sup id="cite_ref-mus_117-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mus-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Old Town of Plovdiv is a historic preservation site known for its Bulgarian Renaissance architectural style. The Old Town covers the area of the three central hills (\xd0\xa2\xd1\x80\xd0\xb8\xd1\x85\xd1\x8a\xd0\xbb\xd0\xbc\xd0\xb8\xd0\xb5, <i>Trihalmie</i>). Almost every house in the Old Town has its characteristic exterior and interior decoration.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed-hover center">\n\t<li class="gallerycaption">The Old
