/></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytextwrapper" style="width: 160px"><div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hindliyan_House&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hindliyan House (page does not exist)">Hindliyan House</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div></div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span id="Churches.2C_mosques_and_temples"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Churches,_mosques_and_temples">Churches, mosques and temples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Churches, mosques and temples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are a number of 19th-century churches, most of which follow the distinctive <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a> construction style. They are the Saint Constantine and Saint Helena, the Saint Marina, the Saint Nedelya, the Saint Petka, and the Holy Mother of God Churches. As the city has been a gathering center for Orthodox Christians for a long period of time, Plovdiv is surrounded by several monasteries located at the foot of the Rhodope Mountains such as "St. George", "St. Kozma and Damian", St. Kirik, and Yulita (Ulita). They remain good examples of the late Middle Age Orthodox architecture and iconography masterpieces typical for the region. There are also Roman Catholic cathedrals in Plovdiv, the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St_Louis,_Plovdiv" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of St Louis, Plovdiv">Cathedral of St Louis</a> being the largest. There are several more modern Baptist, Methodist, Presbyterian, and other Protestant churches, as well as older style <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Apostolic">Apostolic</a> churches. Two mosques remain in Plovdiv from the time of Ottoman rule. The Djumaya Mosque is considered the oldest European mosque outside Moorish Spain.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sephardic" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic">Sephardic</a> <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Synagogue" title="Plovdiv Synagogue">Plovdiv Synagogue</a> is at Tsar Kaloyan Street 13 in the remnants of a small courtyard in what was once a large Jewish quarter. Dating to the 19th century, it is one of the best-preserved examples of the so-called "Ottoman-style" synagogues in the Balkans. According to author Ruth E. Gruber, the interior of the <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Synagogue" title="Plovdiv Synagogue">Plovdiv Synagogue</a> is a "hidden treasure\xe2\x80\xa6a glorious, if run-down, burst of color." An exquisite Venetian glass chandelier hangs from the center of the ceiling, which has a richly painted dome. All surfaces are covered in elaborate, Moorish-style, geometric designs in once-bright greens and blues. Torah scrolls are kept in the gilded Aron-ha-Kodesh.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre_and_music">Theatre and music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Theatre and music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Small_Plovdiv_street.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Small_Plovdiv_street.JPG/200px-Small_Plovdiv_street.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Small_Plovdiv_street.JPG/300px-Small_Plovdiv_street.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Small_Plovdiv_street.JPG/400px-Small_Plovdiv_street.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Small_Plovdiv_street.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A preserved medieval street in the Old town</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Odeon021.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Odeon021.jpg/200px-Odeon021.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Odeon021.jpg/300px-Odeon021.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Odeon021.jpg/400px-Odeon021.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Odeon021.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A performance in the <a href="/wiki/Odeon_of_Philippopolis" title="Odeon of Philippopolis">Roman Odeon</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Plovdiv Drama Theatre<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> is a successor of the first professional theatre group in Bulgaria founded in 1881. The Plovdiv Puppet Theatre, founded in 1948, remains one of the leading institutions in this genre. The Plovdiv Opera was established in 1953.\n</p><p>Another pillar of Plovdiv\'s culture is the Philharmonic, founded in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Soloists such as <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Shostakovich" title="Dmitri Shostakovich">Dmitri Shostakovich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sviatoslav_Richter" title="Sviatoslav Richter">Sviatoslav Richter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mstislav_Rostropovich" title="Mstislav Rostropovich">Mstislav Rostropovich</a>, Yuri Boukov, and Mincho Minchev have worked with the Plovdiv Philharmonic. The orchestra has toured in almost all of the European countries.\n</p><p>The Trakiya Folklore Ensemble, founded in 1974, has performed thousands of concerts in Bulgaria and more than 42 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The Trakiya Traditional Choir was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Detska_Kitka_Choir" title="Detska Kitka Choir">Detska Kitka Choir</a> is one of the oldest and best-known youth choirs in Bulgaria and the winner of numerous awards from international choral competitions. <a href="/wiki/Evmolpeya" title="Evmolpeya">The Evmolpeya choir</a> is another girls\' choir from Plovdiv, whose establishing patron, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Chomakov" title="Ivan Chomakov">Ivan Chomakov</a>, became the then mayor in 2006. The choir was appointed a <a href="/wiki/Goodwill_Ambassador" class="mw-redirect" title="Goodwill Ambassador">Goodwill Ambassador</a> and a municipal choir.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Plovdiv is among the nation\'s primary literary centres. In 1855 <a href="/wiki/Hristo_G._Danov" title="Hristo G. Danov">Hristo G. Danov</a> created the first Bulgarian publishing company and printing-press.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s traditions as a literary centre are preserved by the first public library in Bulgaria, the <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Vazov_National_Library" title="Ivan Vazov National Library">Ivan Vazov National Library</a>, the 19 <i><a href="/wiki/Chitalishta" class="mw-redirect" title="Chitalishta">chitalishta</a></i> (cultural centres), and by numerous booksellers and publishers. The library was founded in 1879<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and named after the famous Bulgarian writer and poet <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Vazov" title="Ivan Vazov">Ivan Vazov</a> who worked in Plovdiv for five years creating some of his best works.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Today the Ivan Vazov National Library is the second largest national library institution with more than 1.5&#160;million books,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> owning rare Bulgarian and European publications.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_Art_Gallery_P5030085.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Plovdiv_Art_Gallery_P5030085.JPG/200px-Plovdiv_Art_Gallery_P5030085.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Plovdiv_Art_Gallery_P5030085.JPG/300px-Plovdiv_Art_Gallery_P5030085.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Plovdiv_Art_Gallery_P5030085.JPG/400px-Plovdiv_Art_Gallery_P5030085.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_Art_Gallery_P5030085.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Art Gallery of Plovdiv</div></div></div>\n<p>The city has traditions in <a href="/wiki/Iconography" title="Iconography">iconography</a> since the Middle Ages. During the Period of National Revival, a number of notable icon-painters (called in Bulgarian <i>zografi</i>, <i>\xd0\xb7\xd0\xbe\xd0\xb3\xd1\x80\xd0\xb0\xd1\x84\xd0\xb8</i>) from all regions of the country worked in Plovdiv such as&#160;&#8211;&#32; <a href="/wiki/Dimitar_Zograf" title="Dimitar Zograf">Dimitar Zograf</a>, his son Zafir Zograf, <a href="/wiki/Zahari_Zograf" title="Zahari Zograf">Zahari Zograf</a>, Georgi Danchov, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-pat_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pat-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> After the Liberation, the Bulgarian painter of <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czech</a> origin <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Mrkvi%C4%8Dka" title="Ivan Mrkvi\xc4\x8dka">Ivan Mrkvi\xc4\x8dka</a> came to work in the city. The Painters\' Society was established there by artists from southern Bulgaria in 1912 whose members included painters <a href="/wiki/Zlatyu_Boyadzhiev" title="Zlatyu Boyadzhiev">Zlatyu Boyadzhiev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsanko_Lavrenov" title="Tsanko Lavrenov">Tsanko Lavrenov</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sirak_Skitnik&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sirak Skitnik (page does not exist)">Sirak Skitnik</a>.\n</p><p>Today the city has more than 40 art galleries with most of them being privately owned. The Art Gallery of Plovdiv was founded in the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> It possesses 5,000 pieces of art in four buildings. Since 1981, it has had a section for <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Mexico" title="Culture of Mexico">Mexican</a> art donated by Mexican painters in honour of the 1,300-year anniversary of the Bulgarian State.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Capital_of_Culture">European Capital of Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: European Capital of Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 5 September 2014, Plovdiv was selected as the Bulgarian host of <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-culturecapital_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culturecapital-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The city will co-host the event with <a href="/wiki/Matera" title="Matera">Matera</a> and another city (yet to be decided).\n</p><p>After Plovdiv was elected as European Capital of Culture in 2019, an ambitious cultural program has started its realisation. According to this program, there will be an Island of Arts in the middle of the Maritsa River in Plovdiv. The "Kapana" area (the "Trap") will become a quarter of the arts where the creative industries are going to be developed and presented. This famous area, Kapana, was renovated in 2014, restoring its authentic outlook. It has been used for a number of festivals and art events, attracting visitors from all over Bulgaria and the world.\n</p><p>For 2019 the City Under the Hills is planning a number of concerts, including "Balkan Music in Plovdiv".The city will host the Plovdiv Biennale and a number of international forums, such as a meeting of collectors from Europe, a summer art school, dance projects, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Plovdiv" title="Economy of Plovdiv">Economy of Plovdiv</a></div>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:blue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:68.454710592869px 72.896862742141px 0 0; border-top-color:green"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:green"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:69.098300562505px; border-width:0 0 30.901699437495px 95.105651629515px; border-bottom-color:red"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>GVA by sector (2013)\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:red; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Agriculture (5%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:green; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;Industry (57%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:blue; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;Services (38%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:aqua"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:99.211470131448px 12.53332335643px 0 0; border-top-color:fuchsia"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:fuchsia"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:87.630668004386px 48.175367410172px 0 0; border-top-color:yellow"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:yellow"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:58.778525229247px 80.901699437495px 0 0; border-top-color:blue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:blue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:12.53332335643px 99.211470131448px 0 0; border-top-color:green"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:green"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:0; border-width:0 82.727194597248px 100px 0; border-right-color:red"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:red"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Employees by sector (2014)\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:red; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Manufacturing (36%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:green; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;Commerce (16%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:blue; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;Education (8%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:yellow; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Healthcare (7%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:fuchsia; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Transport (6%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:aqua; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other (27%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>Although it is located in the middle of a rich agricultural region, Plovdiv\'s economy has shifted from agriculture to industry since the beginning of the 20th century. <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">Food processing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brewing" title="Brewing">brewing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Textiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Textiles">textiles</a> formed the pillars of the industrial economic shift.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communist</a> rule, the city\'s economy expanded and was dominated by heavy industry. After the fall of Communism in 1989 and the collapse of Bulgaria\'s <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economy</a>, a number of industrial complexes were closed; production of lead and <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machinery" class="mw-redirect" title="Machinery">machinery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motor_truck" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor truck">motor trucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemicals</a>, and cosmetics have continued.\n</p><p>Plovdiv is the economic capital of Bulgaria as it has the country\'s largest economy and contributes 7.5% of Bulgaria\'s GDP as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-nsi_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsi-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, more than 35 thousand companies operate in the region which create jobs for 285,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-nsi_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsi-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>  The advantages of Plovdiv include the central geographic location, good infrastructure, and large population. Plovdiv has an international airport, terminal for intermodal transport, several connections with <a href="/wiki/Trakia_motorway" title="Trakia motorway">Trakia motorway</a> (connecting <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burgas" title="Burgas">Burgas</a>), proximity to <a href="/wiki/Maritsa_motorway" title="Maritsa motorway">Maritsa motorway</a> (the main corridor to <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>), and well-developed road and rail infrastructure which all led to the development of the city as the leading city in terms of industrial output in Bulgaria.\n</p><p>The economy of Plovdiv has long tradition in <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commerce" title="Commerce">commerce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transport" title="Transport">transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications">communications</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>. Apart from the industrial development of Plovdiv, there has been a significant surge in the IT and outsourcing service sector in the recent years, as well as a double-digit increase in the tourism growth in the city every year for the past 5 years.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_Indicators">Economic Indicators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economic Indicators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; align="right">1.546\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Source: The National Statistical Institute<sup id="cite_ref-nsi_132-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsi-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Industry has been the sole leader in attracting investment. Industry has been expanding since the late 1990s, with manufacturing plants being built in the city or in its outskirts mainly the municipality of Maritsa. In this period, some \xe2\x82\xac500,000,000 has been invested in the construction of new factories. <a href="/wiki/Trakia_Economic_Zone" title="Trakia Economic Zone">Trakia Economic Zone</a> which is one of the largest industrial zones in Eastern Europe, is located around Plovdiv. Some of the biggest companies in the region include the Austrian utility company <a href="/wiki/EVN_Group" title="EVN Group">EVN</a>, PIMK  (transport), Insa Oil (fuels), <a href="/wiki/Liebherr" title="Liebherr">Liebherr</a> (refrigerator plant), <a href="/wiki/Magna_International" title="Magna International">Magna International</a> (automotive industry), Bella Bulgaria (food manufacturing), Socotab (tobacco processing), <a href="/wiki/ABB_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="ABB Group">ABB Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schneider_Electric" title="Schneider Electric">Schneider Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osram" title="Osram">Osram</a>, Sensata Technologies, etc.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping_and_commerce">Shopping and commerce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Shopping and commerce">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The commercial sector is developing quickly. Shopping centers have been built mainly in the Central district and the district of Trakiya. Those include Shopping Center Grand,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Market Center,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> and two more all on the Kapitan Raycho Street,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Forum in Trakiya, Excelsior, and others. Plovdiv has three large shopping centers: the \xe2\x82\xac40&#160;million Mall of Plovdiv (opened 2009) with a shopping area of 22,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (236,806.03&#160;sq&#160;ft), 11 cinema halls, and parking for 700 cars;<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Markovo tepe Mall (opened 2016);<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> and Plovdiv Plaza Mall which is 6 stories high with 127 000 m<sup>2</sup> area, half of which is the parking lot and the rest is shopping area.\n</p><p>Due to the high demand for business office space, new office and commercial buildings have been built. Several hypermarkets have been built mainly on the outskirts of the city: <a href="/wiki/Metro_AG" title="Metro AG">Metro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaufland" title="Kaufland">Kaufland</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Triumf_(hypermarket)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Triumf (hypermarket) (page does not exist)">Triumf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Praktiker" title="Praktiker">Praktiker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billa_(supermarket)" title="Billa (supermarket)">Billa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mr._Bricolage" title="Mr. Bricolage">Mr. Bricolage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baumax" class="mw-redirect" title="Baumax">Baumax</a>, Technopolis, Technomarket Europa, and others. The main shopping area is the central street with its shops, caf\xc3\xa9s, and restaurants. A number of caf\xc3\xa9s, craftsmen workshops, and souvenir shops are in the Old Town and the small streets in the centre, known among the locals as "The Trap" (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">\xd0\x9a\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbf\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbd\xd0\xb0</span>).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_International_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Plovdiv International Fair">Plovdiv International Fair</a>, held annually since 1892, is the largest and oldest fair in the country and all of southeastern Europe, gathering companies from all over the world in an exhibition area of 138,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (1,485,419.64&#160;sq&#160;ft) located on a territory of 352,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (3,788,896.47&#160;sq&#160;ft) on the northern banks of the Maristsa river.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> It attracts more than 600,000 visitors from many countries.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city has had a duty-free zone since 1987. It has a customs terminal handling cargo from trucks and trains.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed-hover">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 216px"><div style="width: 216px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 214px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a Plovdiv\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div></div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px"><div style="width: 182px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dzhendem.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Dzhendem.jpg/270px-Dzhendem.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Dzhendem.jpg/405px-Dzhendem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Dzhendem.jpg/540px-Dzhendem.jpg 2x" Mall\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div></div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytextwrapper" style="width: 140px"><div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Forum Trakia shopping center\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div></div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_Railway_Station_TB_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Plovdiv_Railway_Station_TB_1.jpg/220px-Plovdiv_Railway_Station_TB_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Plovdiv_Railway_Station_TB_1.jpg/330px-Plovdiv_Railway_Station_TB_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Plovdiv_Railway_Station_TB_1.jpg/440px-Plovdiv_Railway_Station_TB_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2767" data-file-height="2668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_Railway_Station_TB_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Central_railway_station" title="Plovdiv Central railway station">Plovdiv Central railway station</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Plovdiv\'s geographical position makes it an international transport hub. Three of the ten <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_corridors" title="Pan-European corridors">Pan-European corridors</a> run into or near the city: Corridor IV (<a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>-Plovdiv- <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>), Corridor VIII (<a href="/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs" title="Durr\xc3\xabs">Durr\xc3\xabs</a>-Sofia-Plovdiv-<a href="/wiki/Varna,_Bulgaria" title="Varna, Bulgaria">Varna</a>/<a href="/wiki/Burgas" title="Burgas">Burgas</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Corridor_X" title="Pan-European Corridor X">Corridor X</a> (<a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>-Plovdiv-Istanbul).<sup id="cite_ref-trans_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trans-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> A major tourist centre, Plovdiv lies at the foot of the <a href="/wiki/Rhodope_Mountains" title="Rhodope Mountains">Rhodope Mountains</a>, and most people wishing to explore the mountains choose it as their trip\'s starting point.\n</p><p>The city is a major road and railway hub in southern Bulgaria with<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Trakia_motorway" title="Trakia motorway">Trakia motorway</a> (A1) only 5&#160;km (3&#160;mi) to the north. It lies on the important national route from Sofia to Burgas via Stara Zagora. First-class roads lead to Sofia to the west, <a href="/wiki/Karlovo" title="Karlovo">Karlovo</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Asenovgrad" title="Asenovgrad">Asenovgrad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kardzhali" title="Kardzhali">Kardzhali</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Stara_Zagora" title="Stara Zagora">Stara Zagora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haskovo" title="Haskovo">Haskovo</a> to the east. There are <a href="/wiki/Intercity_bus" class="mw-redirect" title="Intercity bus">intercity buses</a> which link Plovdiv with cities and towns all over the country and many European countries. They are based in three <a href="/wiki/Bus_station" title="Bus station">bus stations</a>: South, Rodopi, and North.\n</p><p>Railway transport in the city dates back to 1872 when it became a station on the <a href="/wiki/Lyubimets" title="Lyubimets">Lyubimets</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Belovo,_Bulgaria" title="Belovo, Bulgaria">Belovo</a> railway line. There are railway lines to Sofia, <a href="/wiki/Panagyurishte" title="Panagyurishte">Panagyurishte</a>, Karlovo, <a href="/wiki/Peshtera" title="Peshtera">Peshtera</a>, Stara Zagora, <a href="/wiki/Dimitrovgrad,_Bulgaria" title="Dimitrovgrad, Bulgaria">Dimitrovgrad</a>, and Asenovgrad. There are three <a href="/wiki/Railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway station">railway stations</a>:&#160;&#8211;&#32; <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Central_railway_station" title="Plovdiv Central railway station">Plovdiv Central</a>, Trakia, and Filipovo&#160;&#8211;&#32; as well as a freight station.<sup id="cite_ref-trans_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trans-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bus_in_Plovdiv_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Bus_in_Plovdiv_2006.jpg/220px-Bus_in_Plovdiv_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Bus_in_Plovdiv_2006.jpg/330px-Bus_in_Plovdiv_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Bus_in_Plovdiv_2006.jpg/440px-Bus_in_Plovdiv_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bus_in_Plovdiv_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bus in Plovdiv</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AG280T07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/AG280T07.jpg/220px-AG280T07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/AG280T07.jpg/330px-AG280T07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/AG280T07.jpg/440px-AG280T07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="596" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AG280T07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trolleybus in Plovdiv</div></div></div>\n<p>Plovdiv has a large public transport system<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> including around 29 main and 10 extra bus lines. However, there are no <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trams</a> in the city, and the <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Plovdiv" title="Trolleybuses in Plovdiv">Plovdiv trolleybus system</a> was closed in autumn 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Six bridges span the <a href="/wiki/Maritsa" title="Maritsa">Maritsa</a> river including a railway bridge and a <a href="/wiki/Covered_bridge" title="Covered bridge">covered bridge</a>. There are important road junctions to the south, southwest, and north.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Velomap_plovdiv.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Velomap_plovdiv.png/220px-Velomap_plovdiv.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Velomap_plovdiv.png/330px-Velomap_plovdiv.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Velomap_plovdiv.png/440px-Velomap_plovdiv.png 2x" data-file-width="933" data-file-height="791" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Velomap_plovdiv.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Plovdiv\'s cycling infrastructure<br />Green: built<br />Orange: planned</div></div></div>\n<p>Plovdiv has a well-developed cycling infrastructure which covers almost all districts of the city. The total length of the cycling roads is 60 kilometres (37 miles) (48 kilometres (30 miles) are completed and 12 kilometres (7.5 miles) are under construction). The city has a total of 690 bike parkings.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed-hover center">\n\t<li class="gallerycaption">Cycling Infrastructure</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215.33333333333px"><div style="width: 215.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 213.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Velo6.jpg" data-file-height="576" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<p>The number of registered private automobiles in the city increased from 178,104 in 2005 to 234,298 in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> There are around 658 cars per 1,000 inhabitants<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_airport_-_New_terminal_building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Plovdiv_airport_-_New_terminal_building.jpg/220px-Plovdiv_airport_-_New_terminal_building.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Plovdiv_airport_-_New_terminal_building.jpg/330px-Plovdiv_airport_-_New_terminal_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Plovdiv_airport_-_New_terminal_building.jpg/440px-Plovdiv_airport_-_New_terminal_building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv_airport_-_New_terminal_building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Airport" title="Plovdiv Airport">Plovdiv Airport</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Plovdiv International Airport">Plovdiv International Airport</a> is near the village of <a href="/wiki/Krumovo" title="Krumovo">Krumovo</a>, 5&#160;km (3&#160;mi) southeast of the city. It takes charter flights from Europe and has scheduled services with Ryanair to London and S7 to Moscow. Many small airports are in the city\'s surroundings, including the <a href="/wiki/Graf_Ignatievo_Air_Base" title="Graf Ignatievo Air Base">Graf Ignatievo Air Base</a> in <a href="/wiki/Graf_Ignatievo" title="Graf Ignatievo">Graf Ignatievo</a> to the north of Plovdiv.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/BIAF_Airshow" class="mw-redirect" title="BIAF Airshow">BIAF Airshow</a> is held every two years on the <a href="/wiki/Krumovo" title="Krumovo">Krumovo</a> airbase and is one of the biggest airshows in the Balkans.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="particularly for the">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Around two thirds of the citizens (62,38%) have secondary, specialized, or higher education. That percentage increased from 1992 to 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-edu_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edu-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Plovdiv has 78 schools including elementary, high, foreign language, mathematics, technical, and art schools. There are also 10 private schools and a <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a>. The number of pupils in 2005 was 36,964 and has been constantly decreasing since the mid-1990 due to lower birth rate.<sup id="cite_ref-edu_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edu-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Among the most prestigious schools are the English Language School, the High School of Mathematics, the Ivan Vazov Language School, the National Schools of Commerce&#160;&#8211;&#32; Plovdiv,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> the English Academy,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> the Academy of Music, Dance and Fine Arts Plovdiv,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> and the French High School of Plovdiv.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city has six universities and a number of state and private colleges and branches of other universities. Those include <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Plovdiv University">Plovdiv University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> with 900 lecturers and employees and 13,000 students; the <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Medical_University" title="Plovdiv Medical University">Plovdiv Medical University</a>, with 2,600 students;<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> the Medical College; the Technical University of Sofia&#160;&#8211;&#32;Branch Plovdiv;<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> the Agricultural University&#160;&#8211;&#32; Plovdiv;<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> the University of Food Technologies;<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> the Academy for Music, Dance and Fine Arts;<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-edu_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edu-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2009 <a href="/wiki/International_Olympiad_in_Informatics" title="International Olympiad in Informatics">International Olympiad in Informatics</a> (IOI) was held at the <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Plovdiv University">University of Plovdiv "Paisiy Hilendarski"</a>, between 8 and 15 August 2009. The 2009 IOI Honorary Patron was <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bulgaria" title="President of Bulgaria">Bulgarian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Georgi_Parvanov" title="Georgi Parvanov">Georgi Parvanov</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Between 1875 and 1906, the <a href="/wiki/Zariphios_School" title="Zariphios School">Zariphios School</a> was one of the local Greek educational institutions that provided elementary and secondary education.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_and_recreation">Sports and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sports and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv_Sports_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Plovdiv Sports Complex (page does not exist)">Plovdiv Sports Complex</a> consists of <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Plovdiv Stadium">Plovdiv Stadium</a> with several additional football fields, tennis courts, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_pool" title="Swimming pool">swimming pools</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing base</a> with a 2&#160;km-long channel, restaurants, and caf\xc3\xa9s in a spacious park in the western part of the city just south of the <a href="/wiki/Maritsa" title="Maritsa">Maritsa</a> river. There are also playgrounds for children. It is popular among the citizens and guests of Plovdiv who use it for jogging, walking, and relaxation. Plovdiv Stadium (55,000 seats) is the largest football venue in Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other stadiums include <a href="/wiki/Hristo_Botev_Stadium_(Plovdiv)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hristo Botev Stadium (Plovdiv)">Stadion Botev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lokomotiv_Stadium_(Plovdiv)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lokomotiv Stadium (Plovdiv)">Lokomotiv</a> (10,000 seats), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maritsa_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maritsa Stadium (page does not exist)">Maritsa Stadium</a> (5,000 seats), and <a href="/wiki/Todor_Diev_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Todor Diev Stadium">Todor Diev Stadium</a> (7,000 seats). There are seven indoor <a href="/wiki/Sports_hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports hall">sports halls</a>: <a href="/wiki/Kolodruma" title="Kolodruma">Kolodruma</a>, University Hall, Olimpia, Lokomotiv, Dunav, Stroitel, Chaika, Akademik, and Total Sport. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Aqualand" title="Aqualand">Aqualand</a>, a water park, was opened near the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Several smaller water parks are in the city as well.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed-hover center">\n\t<li class="gallerycaption">Sport Facilities</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytextwrapper" style="width: 160px"><div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Plovdiv University sports hall\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div></div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in the city; Plovdiv has three professional teams. The city has <a href="/wiki/PFC_Botev_Plovdiv" class="mw-redirect" title="PFC Botev Plovdiv">PFC Botev Plovdiv</a>, founded in 1912 and <a href="/wiki/PFC_Lokomotiv_Plovdiv" title="PFC Lokomotiv Plovdiv">PFC Lokomotiv</a>, founded in 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Both teams are a regular fixture in the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_A_Professional_Football_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Bulgarian A Professional Football Group">top Bulgarian league</a>. The rivalry between them is considered to be even more fierce than the one between <a href="/wiki/PFC_Levski_Sofia" title="PFC Levski Sofia">Levski</a> and <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Sofia" title="PFC CSKA Sofia">CSKA</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>. There are two other football clubs in the city \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Maritsa_Plovdiv" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritsa Plovdiv">Maritsa FC</a> (founded in 1921) and <a href="/wiki/Spartak_Plovdiv" class="mw-redirect" title="Spartak Plovdiv">Spartak Plovdiv</a> (1947).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Plovdiv is host of the international <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> tournament "Strandzha" which has taken place since 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, 96 boxers from 20 countries participated in the tournament. There is a <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a> club and a horse base near the city. Plovdiv has several volleyball and basketball teams.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv-tsar-simeon-garden-201704.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Plovdiv-tsar-simeon-garden-201704.jpg/220px-Plovdiv-tsar-simeon-garden-201704.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Plovdiv-tsar-simeon-garden-201704.jpg/330px-Plovdiv-tsar-simeon-garden-201704.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Plovdiv-tsar-simeon-garden-201704.jpg/440px-Plovdiv-tsar-simeon-garden-201704.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4160" data-file-height="2336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plovdiv-tsar-simeon-garden-201704.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view from the "singing fountains" in Tsar Simeon\'s garden.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_Garden_P5030039.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/City_Garden_P5030039.jpg/220px-City_Garden_P5030039.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/City_Garden_P5030039.jpg/330px-City_Garden_P5030039.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/City_Garden_P5030039.jpg/440px-City_Garden_P5030039.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_Garden_P5030039.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view from the City garden.</div></div></div>\n<p>Three of the city\'s seven hills are protected natural territories since 1995. Two of the first parks in Bulgaria are located in the city center &#160;&#8211;&#32; <i>Tsar Simeon garden \xe2\x80\x93 city garden</i>, where the very first work of the Italian sculptor <a href="/wiki/Arnoldo_Zocchi" title="Arnoldo Zocchi">Arnoldo Zocchi</a> could be seen, and <i>Dondukov garden \xe2\x80\x93 old city garden</i>. Some of the larger parks include the <i>Botanical garden</i>, <i>Beli Brezi</i>, <i>Ribnitsa</i>, and <i>Lauta</i>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_citizens">Notable citizens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notable citizens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hristo_stoichkov-2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Hristo_stoichkov-2010.jpg/220px-Hristo_stoichkov-2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="382" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Hristo_stoichkov-2010.jpg/330px-Hristo_stoichkov-2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Hristo_stoichkov-2010.jpg/440px-Hristo_stoichkov-2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="444" data-file-height="770" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hristo_stoichkov-2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hristo_Stoichkov" title="Hristo Stoichkov">Hristo Stoichkov</a></div></div></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Andonov" title="Ivan Andonov">Ivan Andonov</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; (1934\xe2\x80\x932011), actor</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Arabadzhiev" title="Vladimir Arabadzhiev">Vladimir Arabadzhiev</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; (born 1984), racing driver</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rusev_(wrestler)" title="Rusev (wrestler)">Miroslav Barnyashev</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; (born 1984), professional wrestler, performing under the name of Miro</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Zlatyu_Boyadzhiev" title="Zlatyu Boyadzhiev">Zlatyu Boyadzhiev</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; (1903\xe2\x80\x931976), painter</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Boris_Christoff" title="Boris Christoff">Boris Christoff</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; (1914\xe2\x80\x931993), basso</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hristo_G._Danov" title="Hristo G. title="Yekaterinburg">Yekaterinburg</a>, Russia</li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honour">Honour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Honour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">asteroid</a> (<a href="/wiki/Minor_planet" title="Minor planet">minor planet</a>) <a href="/wiki/List_of_minor_planets:_3001%E2%80%934000#860" title="List of minor planets: 3001\xe2\x80\x934000">3860 Plovdiv</a> is named after the city. It was discovered by the <a href="/wiki/Belgian" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian">Belgian</a> astronomer <a href="/wiki/Eric_Walter_Elst" title="Eric Walter Elst">Eric W. Elst</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarian</a> astronomer <a href="/wiki/Violeta_G._Ivanova" title="Violeta G. Ivanova">Violeta G. Ivanova</a> on 8 August 1986. <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv_Peak" title="Plovdiv Peak">Plovdiv Peak</a> (1,040&#160;m or 3,412&#160;ft) on <a href="/wiki/Livingston_Island" title="Livingston Island">Livingston Island</a> in the <a href="/wiki/South_Shetland_Islands" title="South Shetland Islands">South Shetland Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>, is also named after Plovdiv.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
